  │     │                │ schema                                           │

  ────────────────────────────────────────

  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Shared File: packages/core/src/atlas/wires.ts
  Who Touches It: ATLAS Wire (replaces) + Phase 2+3 (references)
  Severity: HIGH — one agent rewrites it, another agent depends on the result
  ────────────────────────────────────────

  Who Touches It: ATLAS Wire + QUE Scope A (registration)
  Severity: MEDIUM — both modify
  ────────────────────────────────────────

  Who Touches It: QUE Scope C + Householding (entity_type)
  Severity: MEDIUM — both extend
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Shared File: apps/prodash/
  Who Touches It: QUE Scope B + Householding UI
  Severity: LOW — different subdirectories

  The Hard Truth

  You cannot run all 6 in parallel. There are real dependency chains that will
  cause agents to make incompatible decisions about shared interfaces.

  The biggest danger isn't merge conflicts (those are fixable) — it's semantic 
  divergence: Agent A defines the ATLAS registry schema one way, Agent B assumes
   a different shape for QUE tool registration, and now you have two
  incompatible architectures that both compiled fine in isolation.

  ---
  Recommended Approach: 2 Waves, 3+3

  Wave 1 — 3 Agents (Fully Independent)

  Agent: W1-A
  Project: Householding (TRK-224)
  Why Safe: Standalone collection, new API routes, new UI. Only adds
  household_id
    to existing client type.
  Est. Size: ~1,200 lines
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Agent: W1-B
  Project: ATLAS Wire Architecture (TRK-13296)
  Why Safe: Self-contained in packages/core/src/atlas/. New super-tools/
    directory. Replaces existing wires. Registry schema update.
  Est. Size: ~870 lines
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Agent: W1-C
  Project: Yellow Phase 2+3 — CALC TOOLS ONLY
  Why Safe: All 25 calc-* and 8 lookup-* tools as pure TypeScript functions. No
    Firestore, no API, no sessions. Just math with typed inputs/outputs.
  Est. Size: ~1,500 lines

  Why these 3 are safe together:
  - Householding touches types/index.ts to add Household interface — ATLAS Wire
  touches it to add SuperTool/Wire types — Phase 2+3 creates calc-* in a brand
  new directory. Three different additions, resolvable merge.
  - Zero shared files between Householding and ATLAS Wire.
  - Calc tools are pure functions in a new directory — zero overlap with
  anything.

  Wave 2 — 3 Agents (After Wave 1 Merges)

  Agent: W2-A
  Project: QUE Scope A — Core + Registry + API
  What It Needs From Wave 1: ATLAS wire schema (from W1-B) for tool
  registration.
    Household types (from W1-A) for session scoping.
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Agent: W2-B
  Project: QUE Scope B — Workbench UI
  What It Needs From Wave 1: QUE types + API routes (from W2-A). Household
  detail
    integration.
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Agent: W2-C
  Project: QUE Scope C — Orchestration + ANALYZE_* super tools + GENERATE_* +
    ASSEMBLE
  What It Needs From Wave 1: Everything. Wires calc tools (W1-C) into ANALYZE_*
    super tools (ATLAS pattern from W1-B). Flow Engine + Pipeline Studio + DEX +

    Householding integration.

  W2-A and W2-B could potentially run in parallel if you define the QUE type
  contracts first (in Scope A's plan) and give Scope B those types as a spec to
  code against. Scope C is the caboose no matter what.

  ---
  Bottom Line

  ┌──────────┬─────────┬───────────────────────────────┬───────────────────┐
  │  Option  │ Agents  │             Risk              │       Speed       │
  ├──────────┼─────────┼───────────────────────────────┼───────────────────┤
  │          │         │ HIGH — semantic conflicts in  │ Fastest           │
  │ 6        │ 6       │ types/index.ts, atlas routes, │ wall-clock if it  │
  │ parallel │         │  flow engine will cost more   │ works, slowest if │
  │          │         │ to fix than running in waves  │  it doesn't       │
  ├──────────┼─────────┼───────────────────────────────┼───────────────────┤
  │ 3 + 3    │ 3 then  │ LOW — each wave is fully      │ Recommended —     │
  │ waves    │ 3       │ independent, Wave 2 has clean │ best risk/reward  │
  │          │         │  foundations                  │                   │
  ├──────────┼─────────┼───────────────────────────────┼───────────────────┤
  │ 3 + 2 +  │ 3 then  │ LOWEST — Scope C runs last    │                   │
  │ 1        │ 2 then  │ with everything done          │ Safest but slower │
  │          │ 1       │                               │                   │
  ├──────────┼─────────┼───────────────────────────────┼───────────────────┤
  │ 2 + 2 +  │ 2 then  │                               │ Too conservative  │
  │ 2        │ 2 then  │ LOWEST — most sequential      │ for what you're   │
  │          │ 2       │                               │ building          │
  └──────────┴─────────┴───────────────────────────────┴───────────────────┘

  My recommendation: 3+3. Wave 1 is your foundation pour. Wave 2 builds the
  house. You get 6 agents total, just staggered by one merge checkpoint. Each
  wave is still fully parallel internally.

  The merge between waves is fast — it's the Planner/Auditor pattern you've
  already proven at scale. Merge Wave 1, cut Wave 2 builders.

✻ Worked for 2m 18s

❯ Well, in that structure, couldn't I give it to one terminal agent for the W-2 
 A, B, and C and say, "Your W-2 runs A, B, and C sequentially"?                 

⏺ Yes — and that's actually better than 3 separate agents for Wave 2.

  Here's why: Scopes A, B, and C are one cohesive system (QUE). The agent that
  builds A's types and API routes has the full mental model when it starts B's
  UI. When it hits C (orchestration), it knows every interface, every route,
  every type it built in A and B. Zero "telephone game" between agents about
  contract shapes.

  Splitting QUE across 3 agents was always the riskiest part of the plan — three
   agents making independent design decisions about one tightly coupled system.

  Revised structure:

  ┌───────────┬───────────────────────────────────────────┬─────────────────┐
  │  Session  │                   What                    │      Mode       │
  ├───────────┼───────────────────────────────────────────┼─────────────────┤
  │ Terminal  │ Householding (TRK-224)                    │ Parallel with 2 │
  │ 1         │                                           │  & 3            │
  ├───────────┼───────────────────────────────────────────┼─────────────────┤
  │ Terminal  │ ATLAS Wire Architecture (TRK-13296)       │ Parallel with 1 │
  │ 2         │                                           │  & 3            │
  ├───────────┼───────────────────────────────────────────┼─────────────────┤
  │ Terminal  │ Yellow Phase 2+3 — Calc + Lookup tools    │ Parallel with 1 │
  │ 3         │ only (pure math)                          │  & 2            │
  ├───────────┼───────────────────────────────────────────┼─────────────────┤
  │ Terminal  │ QUE Scope A → B → C (sequential, one      │ After 1-3 merge │
  │ 4         │ agent)                                    │                 │
  └───────────┴───────────────────────────────────────────┴─────────────────┘

  4 terminal agents. 3 fire now, 1 fires after merge.

  Terminal 4 is your biggest agent — it builds the entire QUE engine end to end.
   But it's also the most context-rich agent you'll have, because it carries its
   own decisions forward through all three scopes. And it inherits clean
  foundations from the first three (household types, ATLAS wire pattern, 33
  calc/lookup tools ready to wire in).

  The merge checkpoint between Wave 1 and Terminal 4 is the only gate. Fast —
  just the Planner/Auditor merge of 3 worktrees, then cut Terminal 4 loose.

  What Each Agent Does

  Each one autonomously:
  1. Creates a git worktree (isolated workspace)
  2. Runs npm install
  3. Creates/finds its FORGE sprint
  4. Discovery — Fetches FORGE prompt via forge-cli.ts, reads discovery doc,
  creates plan, transitions items to planned
  5. Building — Fetches FORGE prompt, executes the plan, type-checks, commits,
  transitions to built
  6. Audit — Fetches FORGE prompt, runs full audit checklist, fixes issues,
  transitions to audited
  7. Pushes branch, STOPS

  Morning Workflow

  1. Wake up → check T1, T2, T3 results
  2. Merge the three branches to main:
  cd ~/Projects/toMachina
  git merge wave1/householding
  git merge wave1/atlas-wire
  git merge wave1/calc-tools
  3. Resolve any type conflicts in packages/core/src/types/index.ts (3-way add)
  4. Hit Enter on T4 → it runs QUE Scope A → B → C sequentially
  5. Audit everything yourself when T4 reports done

⏺ That's the root cause right there.

  "here's a discovery URL, figure it out." The Discovery phase is SUPPOSED to be

  tracker items — that IS the plan. But nothing in the FORGE prompt explicitly
  tells the agent "your job right now is to create 15-90 tracker items from this
   discovery doc." An agent that's never been through the FORGE workflow before
  doesn't know that's what Discovery means.

  The fix is two things:
  1. Never again write custom agent instructions that bypass FORGE. The agents
  get the FORGE prompts, period.
  2. The #LetsPlanIt prompt could include a line like: "Read the discovery
  document. Decompose the scope into individual FORGE tracker items. Each item =
   one trackable deliverable." That makes the Discovery phase self-documenting.

- **TRK-13323** [Feature]: VALIDATE super tool — validate-record →

  Item: TRK-13332

  Real Code?: YES — replaced with WIRE_DEFINITIONS_V2, legacy getWires()
  backward
    compat
  Does What Description Says?: YES — 16 old → 3 new, legacy API preserved

  Critical check — is this drywall or studs?

  Per "The Fight" lesson: does the code EXECUTE or just DESCRIBE?

  - Atomic tools: Real functions with execute() that take typed input and return
   typed output. Not Firestore docs. Not config constants. Callable code.
  - Super tools: Real async functions with execute() that import and call the
  atomic tools. The NORMALIZE super tool actually imports and calls
  normalizeData(), normalizeBoBExecute(), and normalizeStatusExecute() in
  sequence. Real orchestration.
  - Wires: Config arrays — WIRE_DEFINITIONS_V2 is a constant, not executable
  code. getWireSuperTools() returns the sequence but nothing reads and executes
  it automatically.

  This is the same pattern from "The Fight." The tools are real. The super tools
   are real. The wires are config that nothing calls yet. There's no
  orchestrator that reads WIRE_DATA_IMPORT and runs SUPER_EXTRACT →
  SUPER_VALIDATE → SUPER_NORMALIZE → SUPER_MATCH → SUPER_WRITE in sequence.

  BUT — the discovery doc explicitly says this: "The wire is a sequence of Super
   Tool IDs" and the orchestrator that chains them was always planned for the
  ATLAS Drop Zone UI / API route. The wires are the blueprint. The super tools
  are the executables. The orchestrator that reads the blueprint and calls the
  executables is the next layer up (lives in the API route, not in
  packages/core).

  So: not drywall. The studs are there (super tools execute). The wires are the
  architectural drawing that the API route follows. This is the intended
  architecture per the discovery doc.

  Plan Audit Report                                                             
                                                                                
  1. GAPS                                                                       
                                                                                
  GAP-1: No compliance disclosure requirement for Tax Harvesting outputs.       
  The discovery doc explicitly states: "Compliance: All outputs require RPI +   
Signal Advisors Wealth disclosure                                               
  (stored in _instructions.md)." The plan doesn't mention this anywhere. A      
builder could ship Tax Harvesting                                               
  templates and generators without the required compliance footer. This must be 
 added to the Wave 3 template                                                   
  specs for TRK-13424/TRK-13425 and to the generator spec for                   
TRK-13378/TRK-13379.                                                            
                                                                                
  GAP-2: No fallback plan for TRK-13382 (generate-factfinder) if TRK-13430      
(locate factfinder) fails.                                                      
  The plan correctly identifies the dependency but doesn't say what happens if  
the factfinder template is never                                                
  found. Should the builder: (a) skip it, (b) recreate from the Playbook        
description, or (c) defer to next                                               
  sprint? A builder hitting this will stall.                                    
                                                                                
  ---

Claude.AI archive scan. The tickets                                             
  use the FORMAL casework type names. A builder following the plan will create  
the wrong filenames.

  ---                                                                           
  3. AMBIGUITIES                                                                
                                                                                
  AMB-1: Wave 2 items TRK-13391 and TRK-13392 can't be built in Wave 2.         
  The plan correctly notes that GENERATE_CASEWORK and ASSEMBLE_OUTPUT depend on 
 Wave 3 generators, and mentions                                                
  "come back for GENERATE_CASEWORK and ASSEMBLE_OUTPUT after Wave 3." But the   
summary table at the bottom lists                                               
  all 10 items as Wave 2. A builder assigned Wave 2 will think they need to     
deliver 10 items, hit the dependency                                            
  wall on items 9-10, and not know if they should wait or move on. The plan     
should formally split these as "Wave                                            
  2a" (8 ANALYZE_*) and "Wave 2b" (GENERATE_CASEWORK + ASSEMBLE_OUTPUT, after   
Wave 3).                                                                        
                                                                                
  AMB-2: ANALYZE_ROTH (TRK-13388) is buildable despite TRK-13409 being BLOCKED. 
  The plan flags TRK-13409 (ROTH process doc) as BLOCKED, but doesn't clarify   
that TRK-13388 (ANALYZE_ROTH super                                              
  tool) is NOT blocked — it uses calc tools, not the process doc. A builder     
might assume the entire ROTH vertical                                           
   is frozen. Should state explicitly: "ANALYZE_ROTH super tool is NOT blocked  
— only the process doc is."                                                     
                                                                                
  AMB-3: generate-ai3-pdf (TRK-13380) outputs HTML, not PDF.                    
  The plan correctly describes it as producing HTML that DEX converts to PDF.   
But the tool name and ticket say                                                
  "pdf." A builder might try to implement PDF generation directly. The plan     
should add a note: "Despite the name,                                           
   this tool outputs an HTML string. PDF conversion is handled by DEX           
html-to-pdf in ASSEMBLE_OUTPUT."                                                
                                                                                
  ---                                                                           
  4. SCOPE CREEP                                                                
                                                                                
  None. The plan stays within the discovery and ticket boundaries. The          
dependency graph, builder assignment                                            
  strategy, and overnight agent recommendations are reasonable planning         
additions that don't introduce new work.

> **Discovery:**                                                                
_RPI_STANDARDS/reference/collateral/DISCOVERY-YELLOW-STAGE-PHASE2-PHASE3.md     
> **Plan:** .claude/plans/QUE_PHASE23_PLAN.md                                   
                                                                                
Build the casework component and output layers of QUE. 25 calc tools, 8 lookup  
tools, 8 ANALYZE_* super tools, 8 casework types (Income NOW/LATER, Estate MAX, 
 Growth MAX, LTC MAX, ROTH, Tax Harvesting, MGE Detailed), progressive

## QUE Calc Tools                                                               
- [TRK-13345] [Feature] calc-rmd — Required Minimum Distribution. Prior Year    
Value / IRS Uniform Lifetime Factor.                                            
- [TRK-13346] [Feature] calc-gmib — Guaranteed income from benefit base.        
Benefit Base x Payout Rate (by attained age).                                   
- [TRK-13347] [Feature] calc-rollup — Benefit base growth projection. Base x (1 
 + Rollup Rate) per year, simple or compound.                                   
- [TRK-13348] [Feature] calc-surrender-charge — Cost to exit existing product.  
AV x Charge % (by surrender year in schedule).                                  
- [TRK-13349] [Feature] calc-ltcg — Long-term capital gains tax. (Market Value  
- Cost Basis) x Tax Rate.                                                       
- [TRK-13350] [Feature] calc-bonus-offset — Net cost after carrier bonus.       
(Surrender + LTCG) - (Deposits x Bonus %).                                      
- [TRK-13351] [Feature] calc-provisional-income — IRS formula for SS taxation.  
50% SS + Pensions + Wages + Interest + IRA Dist.                                
- [TRK-13352] [Feature] calc-ss-taxation — How much SS is taxable. Apply        
0%/50%/85% brackets on provisional income.                                      
- [TRK-13353] [Feature] calc-federal-tax — Federal income tax. Apply 2025 MFJ   
brackets to taxable income after deduction.                                     
- [TRK-13354] [Feature] calc-state-tax — State income tax. State-specific rate. 
 Iowa = 0% for retirement income.                                               
- [TRK-13355] [Feature] calc-irmaa — Medicare premium surcharge. MAGI bracket   
lookup -> Part B + Part D surcharge.                                            
- [TRK-13356] [Feature] calc-ss-earnings-limit — Pre-FRA earnings impact. $1    
withheld per $2 above limit + months deferred.                                  
- [TRK-13357] [Feature] calc-income-multiplier — Life insurance needs by age.   
Age-based: 20-39=30x, 40-44=25x ... 70+=5x.                                     
- [TRK-13358] [Feature] calc-college-funding — Future cost of college. $35,331  
x (1 + 6.80%)^(18-age) x 4 years.                                               
- [TRK-13359] [Feature] calc-net-outlay — True cost of life insurance. Premium  
Outlay - Cash Value.                                                            
- [TRK-13360] [F                                                                
… +532 lines …                                                                  
 → INTROSPECT → NORMALIZE → MATCH → WRITE. Commission statements (PDFs, CSVs).  
Revenue domain logic. ~30 lines.

## Audit Checklist                                                              
### Plan ↔ Tickets                                                              
For each ticket:                                                                
- [ ] Is there a corresponding section/task in the plan?                        
- [ ] Does the plan's approach correctly address what the ticket asks for?      
- [ ] Are there any tickets the plan ignores or only partially covers?          
                                                                                
### Plan ↔ Discovery                                                            
For each requirement in the discovery:                                          
- [ ] Does the plan address it?                                                 
- [ ] Does the plan's approach match the discovery's intent (not just the       
letter)?                                                                        
- [ ] Has the plan introduced scope that wasn't in the discovery?               
                                                                                
### Plan Quality                                                                
- [ ] Are builders given enough detail to execute without guessing?             
- [ ] Are dependencies between tasks identified?                                
- [ ] Are there any ambiguous instructions that could be misinterpreted?        
                                                                                
## Output Format                                                                
Report findings as:                                                             
1. **GAPS** — Tickets or discovery requirements not covered by the plan         
2. **MISMATCHES** — Plan approach doesn't match what was asked for              
3. **AMBIGUITIES** — Plan instructions that could be misread by a builder       
4. **SCOPE CREEP** — Plan includes work not grounded in discovery or tickets    
5. **PASS** — Plan fully covers all tickets and faithfully represents the       
discovery

QUE foundation: packages/core/src/que/ (types, engine, adapters, comparison),

## QUE Types                                                                    
- [TRK-13433] [Feature] QueSession type — Active quoting session: client_id,    
household_id, product_line, status                                              
(DRAFT/QUOTING/COMPARING/RECOMMENDING/COMPLETE), quotes[], recommendation.      
- [TRK-13434] [Feature] QueQuote type — Individual quote result from a source.  
Source ID, params, results, timestamp.                                          
- [TRK-13435] [Feature] QueRecommendation type — Finalized recommendation with  
rationale, selected products, solution category.                                
- [TRK-13436] [Feature] QueProfile type — Product line config: Life, Annuity,   
Medicare, Investment. Sources, comparison criteria, output templates.           
- [TRK-13437] [Feature] QueSource + QueOutputTemplate types — Source adapter    
config (links to ATLAS source_registry). Output template config (links to DEX   
forms).                                                                         
                                                                                
## QUE Engine                                                                   
- [TRK-13438] [Feature] QUE session state machine — createSession,              
executeQuote, compareQuotes, finalizeRecommendation. State transitions: DRAFT   
-> QUOTING -> COMPARING -> RECOMMENDING -> COMPLETE.                            
- [TRK-13439] [Feature] QUE comparison algorithms — Side-by-side scoring: sort  
by configurable criteria (premium, benefit, fees, rating). Best-value flags,    
lowest-premium flags.                                                           
                                                                                
## QUE Adapters                                                                 
- [TRK-13440] [Feature] CSG Actuarial adapter — refactor into QUE pattern —     
Extract existing medicare-quote.ts into QUE adapter interface. Base adapter     
class + CSG implementation.                                                     
- [TRK-13441] [Feature] Manual entry adapter — Structured manual quote entry    
for Life/Annuity (advisor runs external tool, enters results). Returns          
QueQuote.                                                                       
- [TRK-13442] [Feature] Playwright adapter placeholder — Interface/placeholder  
for future WinFlex, ARW, Index Standard automation. Not functional yet.         
                                                                                
## QUE API                                                                      
- [TRK-13443] [Feature] que.ts — Session CRUD endpoints — POST /sessions        
(create), GET /sessions (list with filters), GET /sessions/:id (full session    
with quotes + recommendation).                                                  
- [TRK-13444] [Feature] que.ts — Execution endpoints — POST                     
/sessions/:id/quote, POST /sessions/:id/compare, POST /sessions/:id/recommend,  
POST /sessions/:id/generate-output.                                             
- [TRK-13445] [Feature] que-admin.ts — Admin CRUD — CRUD for profiles, sources, 
 output templates. POST /sources/:id/test (test adapter connection).

- [TRK-13446] [Feature] QUE Firestore collections + rules — que_profiles,       
que_sources, que_output_templates, que_sessions, que_quotes,

- [TRK-13447] [Feature] QUE seed data — 4 profiles — Seed Life, Annuity,

- [TRK-13448] [Feature] QUE seed data — 11 sources — Seed CSG, WinFlex, ARW,

## Audit Checklist                                                              
For each requirement/feature/bug in the discovery document:                     
- [ ] Is there a matching ticket?                                               
- [ ] Is the ticket type correct (Bug/Enhancement/Feature/Question)?            
- [ ] Is the ticket description accurate and complete?                          
- [ ] Is the component/portal assignment correct?                               
                                                                                
Then check the reverse:                                                         
- [ ] Are there any tickets that have NO basis in the discovery document?       
- [ ] Are there any tickets that misinterpret what the discovery asked for?     
                                                                                
## Output Format                                                                
Report findings as:                                                             
1. **GAPS** — Requirements in discovery with no ticket (create them)            
2. **MISMATCHES** — Tickets that don't match what discovery says (fix them)     
3. **EXTRAS** — Tickets with no basis in discovery (flag for JDM decision)      
4. **PASS** — Everything matches, no gaps found

After discovery audit passes — update items to `disc_audited`:

⏺ Read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

⏺ Found it. Line 148-149 — the search queries Firestore clients collection using
   where('last_name', '>=', clientSearch.trim()).

  The problem: it's searching by last_name field only, using a prefix match.
  When you type "millang" it's looking for last_name >= "millang" and last_name 
  <= "millang\uf8ff". But Firestore string comparisons are case-sensitive. If
  the last_name field stores "Millang" (capital M), searching "millang"
  (lowercase) won't match.

  This is the same pattern everywhere client lookups are broken — case-sensitive
   Firestore prefix queries. The fix is to either:
  1. Search against a lowercased field (last_name_lower)
  2. Or uppercase the search input to match the stored format

  Let me check how the last_name is actually stored.

✻ Worked for 1m 36s

❯ Seriously?! What fucking search bar on earth is case sensitive?!              

⏺ Firestore's. Every string query in Firestore is case-sensitive by default.
  There's no ILIKE or case-insensitive flag. It's the single most common
  Firestore gotcha and it bites everyone.

  The right long-term fix is a last_name_lower field on every client record that
   stores the lowercase version, and all searches query against that. Three of
  the four search components worked around it with title-case conversion — one
  didn't. Now it does.

  Want me to commit and push this batch?

❯ We gotta put that in the Claw.MD for development standards. That's fucking    
brutal!  Honestly, is that genuinely the best long-term solution? That seems    
just crazy                                                                      

⏺ No, the last_name_lower field is not the best solution. It's the common
  workaround but it's ugly — doubles your fields, you have to keep them in sync,
   and it only solves exact prefix matching.

  The real solution for toMachina: search tokens array. One field per client:

  search_tokens: ['millang', 'josh', 'joshmillang', 'jmillang']

  Firestore's array-contains is case-insensitive by design because you control
  what goes in the array. One field handles first name, last name, full name,
  and any aliases. The normalizer generates the tokens on every write. Done.

  But that's a data model change — every client record needs the field, plus a
  migration to backfill. Sprint 11 or a dedicated ticket.

  For now, the title-case conversion works because your normalizer already
  stores names as title case consistently. The CLAUDE.md rule prevents anyone
  from writing a raw case-sensitive query again.

  Let me add it.

⏺ Here's the full picture:

  ---
  Two Carrier Name Systems — Why They Don't Match

  1. carriers collection (200 docs)

  Created: Sprint 1 data migration (March 9-10, 2026)
  Source: _CARRIER_MASTER tab in RAPID_MATRIX Google Sheets → migrated to
  Firestore
  What it is: A reference/lookup table of carrier brands. Each doc has name
  (parent brand like "Mutual of Omaha"), product_types (what they sell),
  aliases, carrier_type, domain.
  Who reads it: services/api/src/routes/carriers.ts (carrier CRUD API), ATLAS
  registry (carrier grid view), route-to-collection tool, and now the New
  Account modal.
  Schema: { name: "Kansas City Life", product_types: '["Term Life","Whole 
  Life","FIA","MYGA"]', aliases: '[]', ... }

  2. carrier_name field on account subcollection docs

  Created: Multiple sources over time:
  - Sprint 1 Sheets migration (_source: 'sheets_migration') — carried over
  whatever was in the MATRIX Sheets
  - GHL bulk import (March 16) — brought in raw GHL carrier names
  - T5 Medicare Carrier sprint — enriched with charter compound names like
  "AETNA (ACC)- ACCENDO"
  - Manual account creation — whatever someone typed in

  What it is: The actual carrier name stored ON each individual account record
  as a flat string field.
  Who reads it: Everything — CAM revenue, Access Center, account grids, ATLAS
  sources, import routes, QUE engine.
  Schema: Just a string: "Mutual of Omaha" or "Mutual of Omaha (UO)- United of 
  Omaha" or "AETNA (PDP)"

  Why They Don't Match

  The carriers collection has parent brand names: "Mutual of Omaha", "Aetna",
  "Kansas City Life"

  The carrier_name on accounts has whatever came in from the source: charter
  names, compound names, GHL formatting, abbreviations, aliases. The same
  carrier shows up as:
  - "Mutual of Omaha" (parent)
  - "Mutual of Omaha (MUT)- Mutual of Omaha" (charter compound)
  - "Mutual of Omaha (OIC)- Omaha Insurance Company" (different charter)
  - "Mutual of Omaha (UO)- United of Omaha" (another charter)
  - "Mutual of Omaha (UW)- United World" (yet another)

  Nobody ever reconciled them. The carriers collection was seeded from the
  Sheets reference table. The account data was imported from live carrier feeds,
   GHL, and manual entry. T5's Medicare Carrier work added the charter compound
  format intentionally (that's the two-layer identity), but that format doesn't
  match the parent brand names in the carriers collection.

  The Fix

  The carrier_name on accounts should link to carrier_id in the carriers
  collection via a foreign key — not be a loose string. T5 already added
  carrier_id and parent_carrier fields to the Account type. The charter map
  (carrier-charter-map.ts) resolves any name format to a canonical carrier
  identity.

  For the New Account dropdown, the right source is the carriers collection
  (parent brands) since that's what the team knows carriers by. The account's
  carrier_name should be set from the selected carrier's name field, and
  carrier_id set from its doc ID. The charter-level detail gets resolved later
  during the ATLAS import pipeline.

  ---
  Want me to update the modal to use the carriers collection name field (which
  DOES include Kansas City Life) and also set carrier_id on the new account doc?
   Or is there a different approach you want?

⏺ There's your answer.

  Two sources brought in 92% of your accounts with barely any detail:

  Source: sheets_migration (46%)
  Accounts: 920
  What It Had: carrier_name, status, account_type_category
  What It Didn't: Mostly missing: effective_date, cash_value, face_value,
    premium. These came from RAPID_MATRIX which was a tracking sheet, not a
    policy detail system.
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Source: ghl_export_20260316 (46%)
  Accounts: 913
  What It Had: carrier_name, status
  What It Didn't: Almost nothing else. GHL is a CRM — it tracks contacts, not
    policy details. It had carrier name and maybe a policy number. No dates, no
    values, no premiums.

  The other 8% (atlas-wire, KCL scrape, Wellmark report, CoF import) actually
  have rich data because they came from carrier-specific feeds that include
  policy details.

  Why the fields are empty: The two bulk imports that make up 92% of your
  accounts came from systems that don't store policy-level detail. GHL knows
  "Bob Abbott has a policy with Mutual of Omaha" but not the policy number,
  effective date, cash value, or premium. RAPID_MATRIX was the same — a tracking
   ledger, not a contract management system.

  Where the real data lives: In the carrier portals themselves, in the DTCC
  feeds, in the in-force illustrations, and in the physical statements in the
  ACF folders. That data was never imported because there was no automated
  pipeline to pull it — which is exactly what ATLAS + QUE + the carrier adapters
   (WinFlex, Ameritas portal scraping, etc.) are being built to solve.

  This is the Blue Stage → Yellow Stage gap. Blue Stage (ATLAS) gets the data
  in. The data just isn't in yet for 92% of accounts.
